Saturday, 22 June 2013 at 17:21 UTC+02
Ryan Hellyer shared a link.
I usually try to avoid posting uber nerdy stuff on Facebook, but this is something which affects all of you so I'll make an exception. http://geek.ryanhellyer.net/2013/06/23/prism/ I don't think there's any reason to be afraid, but I think it is critically important to be very careful exactly what you put online. My general rule of thumb is that if I'm not prepared to deal with the ramifications of what I do online becoming public, then I just don't do it. I slip up sometimes, but not often. If I need to send something in private, then I use Cryptocat (https://crypto.cat/) which was recommended to me by Thomas Hedderwick.

I plan to do the Oslo marathon in September. I tend to only exercise once per month, usually by running somewhere between 15 and 20 km. Yesterday I decided to cycle 50 km instead. Then today I felt that wasn't enough so I decided to do a short 6 km run as well. But then I felt hungry as I walked out the door, so I stopped at the local shop and bought three doughnuts and two chocolate bars. After 5 km of running, my stomach was churning so much I had to stop. I suspect I need a better training regime :/

Ryan Hellyer updated his status.
In Norwegian, the word "rumpe" means "bum" and the word "troll" means, well, troll. When you jam the two words together you get a combination of what the two individual words mean. So "rumpetroll" should mean "butt troll". So in that case, why the hell do they sell "rumpetroll" in pet shops here in Oslo?

Last week was rather shitty for me. I lost a bunch of money through no fault of my own (well partially, but it wasn't all my fault) and a bunch of other crap went wrong. Thankfully, this afternoon I managed to find a small room in the basement of a building, where this dude happily sold me a product which neatly solved my problem. I paid him a bunch of money, he transferred the goods to me and now I have the solution I needed sitting in my pocket! Yay for me :)

Wednesday, 10 October 2012 at 09:10 UTC+02
Ryan Hellyer updated his status.
I'm on a food rampage this evening ... What the hell is in Norwegian milk that is making me sick? The day I arrived in Norway I became ill. It took me a month to realise it was the milk. I thought maybe I had just become allergic to it over time and not noticed. I've discovered I can have Norwegian lactose free milk, but not regular milk. Even a tiny amount of non-lactose free milk makes me ill. Fast forward a while, and I arrived in Portugal. I accidentally had a giant milkshake, which would normally make me violently ill. It did nothing to me. So I had another one a few days later, and another. Still no ill effects. Back to Norway ... small glass of regular milk. BAM! My stomach was making all sorts of noises it should not be making! Any ideas? I'm running out of explanations for my milk issues.

Friday, 4 May 2012 at 16:59 UTC+02
Ryan Hellyer shared a link.
http://www.guardian.co.uk/world/2012/may/03/possum-tree-drinking-game-dunedin If the powers that be are worried about possuming, then I think they are barking up the wrong tree. They're failing to realise there is a built in safety mechanism ... the urge to pee. At some point you need to climb down to take a leak. At that point, you realise you are too drunk to climb back up. Problem solved. Stupid media trying to find a problem which does not exist. We've been doing far worse crap for as long as I can recall. Nothing has changed. The only change I have seen is that the media like to glamourise stupid harmless student antics these days. Move along, roll along, nothing to see here.

Sunday, 18 March 2012 at 13:11 UTC+01
Ryan Hellyer updated his status.
So I have taken up running it seems. I am not very good at it and I don't like it. The last time I attempted to run anywhere was during the mid-1990's and I did not like it one little bit. I need to run because there isn't really anything better I can do until my shoulder is healed. I also volunteered to compete in a 10 km run in late April. I was originally aiming to finish the 10 km without dying, but since starting running I have discovered two things, firstly, I am fitter than I thought. I pounded out 3.4 km last week after having done no exercise whatever since around August last year (and very little in the six months before that). Secondly, Dr Bret Dougherty appears to have been correct in that I have a mild case of asthma. Bret gave me some inhalers to try out last year and I only got around to using them properly this evening. I decided to go for a light run and head home before I felt too tired ( as opposed to running till I dropped like last week). I barely broke a sweat, yet managed to churn out 3.0 km very easily (http://www.gmap-pedometer.com/?r=5354786). In the interests of not munting myself I'm trying to take it easy and avoid over-doing it. I am concerned though about the issues of shin splints etc. I've had shin splints before, albeit not from running. When I've had shin splints before it has usually been from walking up and down hills for more than 20 km per week for about a month on end. I assume that sort of injury is easier to acquire when running though so I'm keen to avoid anything like that if possible. Simen Thorsrud suggested I run on soft ground, so I jogged along the road to the stream near my house thinking that the surface of the path was soft, but it seems it is actually asphalt (I hadn't been on it since the snow melted). It turns out that I'm not actually aware of any non-asphalt paths around Oslo. What paths I did think were soft, were just asphalt obscured by snow last time I'd been on them (the snow has melted now). So ... any tips on where to run and how to avoid injuries for a novice runner?

Dear Facebook friends, I wanted to send some sort of holiday greeting to my friends and colleagues, but it is difficult in today's world to know exactly what to say without offending someone. So I met with my lawyer yesterday, and on advice I wish to say the following: Please accept with no obligation, implied or implicit, my best wishes for an environmentally conscious, socially responsible, low stress , non addictive, gender neutral celebration of the summer solstice holiday practiced with the most enjoyable traditions of religious persuasion or secular practices of your choice with respect for the religious / secular persuasions and / or traditions of others, or their choice not to practice religious or secular traditions at all. I also wish you a fiscally successful, personally fulfilling and medically uncomplicated recognition of the onset of the generally accepted calendar year 2012, but not without due respect for the calendar of choice of other cultures whose contributions to society have helped make our country great ( not to imply that New Zealand is necessarily greater than any other country ) and without regard to the race, creed, colour, age, physical ability, religious faith or sexual preference of the wishee. By accepting this greeting, you are accepting these terms: This greeting is subject to clarification or withdrawal. It is freely transferable with no alteration to the original greeting. It implies no promise by the wisher to actually implement any of the wishes for her / him or others and is void where prohibited by law, and is revocable at the sole discretion of the wisher. The wish is warranted to perform as expected within the usual application of good tidings for a period of one year or until the issuance of a new wish at the sole discretion of the wisher. Best Regards ( without prejudice ) Name withheld ( Privacy Act ).

Ryan Hellyer posted something via SGPlus.
I wanted spare micro USB cable for my phone, so I went to Dick Smith Electronics only to find that they charge NZ$40 per cable. So I figured I'd check out eBay and thankfully they sold packs of three for 99c including shipping, yay! Except they just arrived .... they do work ... they charge my phone and I can transfer data over them ... except, well, my phone USES more power than they charge it with. So if I leave my phone on the charge for a whole day on one of them, it will eventually go flat. I guess this is a good lesson in why not to be a cheap skate ... I'm now going to pay at least $1 per cable and see how that goes.

For those of you who don't know how to continue torrenting your (legal) files, forget proxies, VPNs and the other bullshit I have heard in the last week like "encrypting your IP address". For those of you who don't like seeing ads or despise Facebook, sign up for Google+ and try the Start G+ Chrome App. I'm using it right now and it's pretty sweet for utilizing Facebook without actually visiting the site at all. Yay :) EDIT: Now that I think of it, it might still be necessary to go there to visit photos sometimes, but you can at least avoid it for viewing the general FB stream, posting stuff (like I'm doing right now) and replying to people.

Ryan Hellyer updated his status.
Thanks for the all the birthday wishes :) My birthday was on 23rd July BTW. Since everyone keeps asking ... I leave the date incorrect for security reasons. Many services, including banks, use your date of birth for doing security checks. So by adding an incorrect date it stymies anyone attempting to use your Facebook profile data for identity theft.

Thursday, 30 August 2007 at 03:50 UTC+02
Miriam Schwab wrote on your timeline.
I couldn't remember how I did it, but now I figured it out. See on the left it says "Applications," and underneath it says Groups, Photos, etc.? See it says "More"? Click on that, and then it says "Notes." Click on that, and then at the top there is a tab that says "My Notes." On that page, on the right-hand side, there is a link that says something like "Edit settings." In there, you can set it up so that your notes are actually your feed from your blog. This will be helpful to you since then you can concentrate on updating your blog, and know that your facebook friends will be updated too. Tell me if you have any problems or if I didn't explain this properly. See, you can only import one RSS feed, which is probably ok for most normal people, but fanatics like me with my three (and soon maybe 4!) blogs could use a way to get more stuff coming in. Maybe that's where that WordPress plugin you mentioned could come in handy.
